What are the accessibility implications of the alt attribute?

How does loading="lazy" affect Largest Contentful Paint (LCP) in Core Web Vitals?

Can CSS override width and height from the <img> tag? ^gRXweBup

1. ¬øC√≥mo explicar√≠a esto de forma precisa en una frase?
2. ¬øQu√© problema o fen√≥meno describe este concepto?
3. ¬øCu√°l es la condici√≥n m√≠nima para que este concepto exista?
4. ¬øCu√°les son sus componentes necesarios y c√≥mo se relacionan?
5. Dibujar todo esto en un esquema entendible  para que la definici√≥n se guie a traves de este sentido ^rzhGaMFs

<img src="photo.jpg" alt="A mountain landscape" width="600" height="400">

<img src="logo.svg" alt="Company logo" loading="lazy">

<img src="map.png" alt="World map" width="300" height="200" loading="eager"> ^dt5z2YTn

src: URL of the image

alt: fallback description

width: horizontal dimension in pixels

height: vertical dimension in pixels

loading: image load strategy ^paoQIsZA

Omitting alt in meaningful images breaks accessibility standards

Using width and height without matching aspect ratio may distort images

Assigning an incorrect or unsupported value to loading results in fallback to default ^WrB7wY98

alt is descriptive text, not a tooltip (unlike title).

width and height set rendered size, not file size.

loading="lazy" improves performance on scroll-heavy pages; not suitable for critical images. ^zvq1is4d

The <img> element in HTML embeds external images into a document, using a set of core attributes to define source location, fallback text, and loading behavior.

The src attribute specifies the image's URL and is mandatory; without it, the image cannot be displayed. 

The alt attribute provides descriptive alternative text used when the image fails to load or for screen readers, and is required for accessibility compliance. 

The width and height attributes define the displayed dimensions of the image and help the browser allocate space before the image is loaded, reducing layout shifts. 

The loading attribute defines the loading behavior, with values such as "lazy" for deferred loading and "eager" for immediate loading, optimizing page performance and resource usage. ^E3CFaT4p

- [ ]  2.1.1 What is Logic in Math Terms?  üõ´   - üìÖ  - ‚è≥ ^gJddyiIn

Common Errors ^k5gwZZkt

Distinctions ^qqYfV01Z

Subvalues of loading attribute in <img>

lazy

Meaning: The image is deferred from loading until it is close to entering the viewport (visible area of the browser).

Use Case: Improves performance by not loading off-screen images immediately.

Effect: Reduces page load time and bandwidth usage, especially useful for long pages with many images.

Supported: ‚úÖ Widely supported in modern browsers.

Example:
<img src="cat.jpg" alt="Cat" loading="lazy">

eager

Meaning: The image is loaded immediately, regardless of whether it is visible or not.

Use Case: Use this for images that are critical to initial rendering, like logos or hero images.

Effect: Increases priority of image loading.

Supported: ‚úÖ Widely supported.

Example:
<img src="banner.jpg" alt="Banner" loading="eager">

auto (default if no loading is set)

Meaning: The browser decides the loading behavior.

Use Case: Let the browser optimize based on its own internal logic.

Effect: Unpredictable; may behave like eager or lazy depending on context.

Supported: ‚úÖ It's the default behavior. ^EwDFyQFy
